  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_914ac30d-09d1-4555-b78c-0dec34b3fa24'

And on top of all that, there’s still more to deal with: a major earthquake, boy confusion, and friends who turn out to be not so friendly. This coming-of-age true story is sure to resonate with anyone who has ever been in middle school, and especially those who have ever had a bit of their own dental drama.</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It's a story written by an adult about her experience as a kid/teenager. I found it very easy to understand. If you can't understand it, it's likely b<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It's a story written by an adult about her experience as a kid/teenager. I found it very easy to understand. If you can't understand it, it's likely because you're not in the right age group it's aimed at, or because it's not at your reading level. Maybe try reading it again later. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div id="review_149670342" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/149670342" />
    <a title="Cate Levinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3394615-cate-levinson"><img alt="Cate Levinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1268857374p2/3394615.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/149670342?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cate Levinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cate Levinson" href="/user/show/3394615-cate-levinson">Cate Levinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer149670342" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9937962333713692818">Poet Ogden Nash said, "Some tortures are physical/And some are mental,/But the one that is both/Is dental."<br/><br/>Graphic Novelist Raina Talgemeier knows this all too well; she is the Odysseus of modern dentistry. The author tells of her own particular journey of adolescent woe which came in the form of a seemingly endless tangle of dentists, endontists, periodontists, orthodonists, with their promises to perfect her not-so pearly whites.<br/><br/>In sixth grade Tanglemeier got braces to fix a run-of-the-mill ov</span>
  <span id="freeText9937962333713692818" style="display:none">Poet Ogden Nash said, "Some tortures are physical/And some are mental,/But the one that is both/Is dental."<br /><br />Graphic Novelist Raina Talgemeier knows this all too well; she is the Odysseus of modern dentistry. The author tells of her own particular journey of adolescent woe which came in the form of a seemingly endless tangle of dentists, endontists, periodontists, orthodonists, with their promises to perfect her not-so pearly whites.<br /><br />In sixth grade Tanglemeier got braces to fix a run-of-the-mill overbite. Then, while horsing around with her friends, she fell, and knocked out her two front teeth. This one misstep plunged her into a four-year ordeal of painful procedures, torturous surgeries, not-to-mention a perpetually changing appearance at a time when every kid is having a crisis of confidence. (As if puberty isn't traumatic enough!) Follow this lost heroine as she battles pimples, overcomes destructive friendships with hypercritical mean girls, endures painful oral surgeries, and finally finds her way to feeling at home in her own skin when she reaches high school.<br /><br />In a particularly wonderful moment, Raina rebukes her long-time "friends" who do nothing but tear her down and tease her. She realizes no friends are better than those friends. Of course she adrift and lonely for a while, but Raina makes new friends soon enough.<br /><br />The moment-of-truth comes when Raina is finally freed from her brace-faced prison. Despite all she has endured, the results are far from perfect. Dreading what she has come to expect as inevitable teasing in response to each dental iteration, she approaches her friends with trepidation. But these new friends are nothing like the petty old friends. They're like, "you look cute... let's go eat!" Phew! These new amigos are actually fun to be around. What's more they love and support her. And with that they wander off into a bright future. This is a must-read for anyone who has ever gone through puberty; you know who you are. Welcome home weary traveler!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9937962333713692818" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_826308437" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/826308437" />
    <a title="Idarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1283951-idarah"><img alt="Idarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596863879p2/1283951.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/826308437?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Idarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Idarah" href="/user/show/1283951-idarah">Idarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780545132060" href="/book/show/6764756-smile">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1283951-idarah?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1283951-idarah?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1283951-idarah?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1283951-idarah?shelf=memoir-bio">memoir-bio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1283951-idarah?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer826308437" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7287069105470758297">Smile is a memoir graphic novel that centers around Telgemeier's traumatic orthodontic experience. Although this book has been making the popularity rounds on YouTube and in other YA circles, it didn't really appeal to me until a booktuber I follow, who isn't a reader of YA books, mentioned a few things that piqued my interest. Coupled with the fact that I myself have been experiencing a dental nightmare since November, I figured I was primed to appreciate this book.<br/><br/>First things first, you don't</span>
  <span id="freeText7287069105470758297" style="display:none">Smile is a memoir graphic novel that centers around Telgemeier's traumatic orthodontic experience. Although this book has been making the popularity rounds on YouTube and in other YA circles, it didn't really appeal to me until a booktuber I follow, who isn't a reader of YA books, mentioned a few things that piqued my interest. Coupled with the fact that I myself have been experiencing a dental nightmare since November, I figured I was primed to appreciate this book.<br /><br />First things first, you don't really need to know too much about the plot, because it really will ruin it for you. Trust me. Here are a few things that may motivate you to give this book a second glance. (1) Don't be fooled by the bright red "Scholastic" imprint on the cover. This is book that will appeal to people of all ages. In fact, it's kinda like Shrek. Anyone can appreciate it, but if you're over 21 and enjoy snarky humor, then you will love it doubly! That kind of leads to the next point. (2) If you are part of Generation Y or an aficionado of the 80s and early 90s, then you will so appreciate the trip down memory lane. The attention to fashion, technology, and pop culture was so awesome! (3) It's set in San Francisco. Hello, dream place to live. Need I say more? The good news is that Telgemeier is working on a followup to this memoir series entitled Sisters. So looking forward to it!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7287069105470758297" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3170412121" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Ines" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43642795-ines"><img alt="Ines" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542692123p2/43642795.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ines" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ines" href="/user/show/43642795-ines">Ines</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3170412121" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7657313189758227891">WONDERFUL!! My daughter and I have enjoyed so much this autobiographical graphic novel.... Raina is a nice little girl, struggling with a crazy fear; that her severe teeth's trauma could compromise her friendships, school experiences and normal social relationships.<br/>But, how it will end!??.<br/>Beautiful, simple and immediate story to read, my daughter was hooked by Raina from the very first page.<br/>We will definitely read the other chapters, too!!<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1580810145i/28901069.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>MERAVIGLIOSO!! io e mia figlia ci siamo godute tantissimo</span>
  <span id="freeText7657313189758227891" style="display:none">WONDERFUL!! My daughter and I have enjoyed so much this autobiographical graphic novel.... Raina is a nice little girl, struggling with a crazy fear; that her severe teeth's trauma could compromise her friendships, school experiences and normal social relationships.<br>But, how it will end!??.<br>Beautiful, simple and immediate story to read, my daughter was hooked by Raina from the very first page.<br>We will definitely read the other chapters, too!!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1580810145i/28901069.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>MERAVIGLIOSO!! io e mia figlia ci siamo godute tantissimo questa graphic novel autobiografica.....Raina è una ragazzina simpatica, alle prese con una paura pazzesca; che il suo grave trauma ai denti possa comprometterle le amicizie, esperienze scolastiche e le normali relazioni sociali.<br>E invece.....<br>Storia bella, semplice e di lettura immediata,a mia figlia è rimasta subito simpatica Raina.<br>Leggeremo sicuramente anche gli altri capitoli!!</span>

<div id="review_275643082" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/275643082" />
    <a title="Victoria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7178730-victoria"><img alt="Victoria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1323845615p2/7178730.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/275643082?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Victoria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Victoria" href="/user/show/7178730-victoria">Victoria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer275643082" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4101539087241181057">Smile<br/><br/>Smile is a comic book by Raina Telgemeier that is funny, sad, touching and very moving. about a girl named Raina who just wants to fit in like everyone else and be a normal sixth grader. But one night, after her girl scout meeting, she trips an falls. This causes her two front teeth to be seriously injured. This only gets worse when it leads problems one after another. Raina is constantly getting her Braces taken on and off of her again, she get’s surgery, a retainer with fake teeth attache</span>
  <span id="freeText4101539087241181057" style="display:none">Smile<br /><br />Smile is a comic book by Raina Telgemeier that is funny, sad, touching and very moving. about a girl named Raina who just wants to fit in like everyone else and be a normal sixth grader. But one night, after her girl scout meeting, she trips an falls. This causes her two front teeth to be seriously injured. This only gets worse when it leads problems one after another. Raina is constantly getting her Braces taken on and off of her again, she get’s surgery, a retainer with fake teeth attached, and just when you think that it couldn’t get any worse she is forced to wear extremely embarrassing headgear! While she has to deal with her dental problems, she has many more things to worry about, a major earthquake, boys, and friends who eventually turn out to be not so nice. <br /><br />The thing that I liked the most about this book is that , it is a true story written by the author about the author’s teenage experiences from Middle School through High School. The book is also illustrated by the author. This means that it’s very original, because every teenager or child could relate tremendously. Raina Telgemeier has captured the highs and lows of being a teenager perfectly through her brilliantly illustrated comics. She has made the truth obvious that it’s not easy being a teenager, and that everybody at some point goes through something similar.<br /><br />One of my favorite two scenes was when Raina was angry about the fact that the dentist was going to pull out her teeth, in order to move the rest of her top teeth toward the center. But when her mom invites her to come along with her sister to watch “The Little Mermaid” in the Cinemas. And since Raina was still grumpy about her teeth she acted as if she was reluctant to go. So when she’s inside the Cinema and waiting for the movie to begin, she thinks “Whatever. I’m too old for this Disney stuff. I’m totally gonna Hate this movie. I just know it. I’m totally gonna..........”. But the minute the movie and music starts , Raina becomes completely engrossed and enchanted with The little Mermaid. When the movie finally ends, she leaves the cinema still thinking about the movie. And way after the movie has ended, at least a week later, she is still obsessed about it. Because of the movie, Raina tells her friend “I finally know what I want to be when I grow up! And animator!”. <br /><br />I like this scene because it was funny but interesting at the same time. Raina first comes into the cinema with the mindset that the movie is going to be completely uninteresting, but leaves the cinema completely spellbound with the movie and mermaids. These scene shows you that you shouldn’t always judge things before you know the full story. <br /><br />The second of my favorite scenes was when Raina was waiting in line to get a snack, her two friends Nicole and Karin pulled her skirt down when she was’t looking.In a matter of seconds the eyes of the school were glued on her. Raina panics and runs into the girls bathroom sobbing. Eventually her friends come into the girl’s bathroom to get her to come back out. But Nicole and Karin couldn’t stop laughing when Raina comes out. It finnally reached to the boiling point where Raina couldn’t take it any more and stood up for herself. Here is a part of the scene where Raina stands up for herself.<br /><br /><br /><br />Raina: You guys want a reaction from me? Fine: Karin, I am NOT a dog, Nicole I am NOT a vampire. <br />Nicole: Oh C’mon I haven’t called you that since--<br />Raina: And I am NOT going to let the rest of you disrespect me anymore! I’m done, GOOD-BYE!<br /><br /><br />I like this scene because, her friends have been teasing and putting her down for the past few years and Raina had to tolerate it. But when it had gone too far, she stood up for what was right. Every time her friends insulted her, it kind of made them feel better about themselves in some kind of twisted way. But just by standing up to her friends, it took away their “power” and pride of hurting her feelings. I really admire her for doing that. Because of what Raina did, she has inspired and taught me that, sometimes you have to be brave and let go of things in order to move forward.<br /><br /><br />Overall this book was amazing. It’s one of the best comic books that I’ve ever read, Raina Telgemeier has really captured the true feelings and emotions that every teenager goes experiences, through engaging illustrations. This book is extremely inspirational, has a lot of lessons to be learnt from it and I highly recommend it 5 stars out of 5. Remember, you don’t have to wear braces to enjoy this book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4101539087241181057" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3045882994" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9884821662741721492">Smile (Smile #1), Raina Telgemeier<br/>Smile is an autobiographical graphic novel written by Raina Telgemeier. It gives an account of the author's life from sixth grade to high school. Raina just wants to be a normal sixth grader. But one night after Girl Scouts she trips and falls, severely injuring her two front teeth, and what follows is a long and frustrating journey with on-again, off-again braces, surgery, embarrassing headgear, and even a retainer with fake teeth attached. And on top of all th</span>
  <span id="freeText9884821662741721492" style="display:none">Smile (Smile #1), Raina Telgemeier<br />Smile is an autobiographical graphic novel written by Raina Telgemeier. It gives an account of the author's life from sixth grade to high school. Raina just wants to be a normal sixth grader. But one night after Girl Scouts she trips and falls, severely injuring her two front teeth, and what follows is a long and frustrating journey with on-again, off-again braces, surgery, embarrassing headgear, and even a retainer with fake teeth attached. And on top of all that, there’s still more to deal with: a major earthquake, boy confusion, and friends who turn out to be not so friendly. This coming-of-age true story is sure to resonate with anyone who has ever been in middle school, and especially those who have ever had a bit of their own dental drama. <br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز دوازدهم ماه مارس سال 2019 میلادی<br />عنوان: لبخندها؛ نویسنده: رینا تلگمایر؛ مترجم: هدی نژادحسینیان؛ ویرایش: نیما مهدیزاده اشرفی؛ تهران: نشر اطراف، راه راه، ‏‫1397؛ در 180 ص؛ شابک: 9786226194068؛ موضوع: داستانهای تصویری از نویسندگان و کارتونیستهای ایالات متتحده آمریکا - سده 20 م‬<br /><br />کتاب «لبخندها» که «رینا تلگمایر» بر اساس یادمانهای کودکی خویش از کلاس ششم تا دبیرستان، و ماجراهای اورتودنسی دندان‌هایش نگاشته و تصویرسازی کرده، یکی از پرفروشترین کتاب‌های مصور نوجوانانه‌ ی فهرست نیویورک‌ تایمز است. از دیگر جایزه‌ های این کتاب می‌توان به جایزه‌ ی «ویل آیزنر» برای بهترین اثر نوجوانان اشاره کرد. نویسنده و تصویرگر این کتاب، «رینا تلگمایر»، یکی از کارتونیست‌های شناخته‌ شده‌ ی نسل جدید است که با تصویرسازی مجموعه‌ کتاب مصور باشگاه پرستاران بچه و بعد با نوشتن و تصویرسازی کتاب لبخندها شناخته شد. «رینا تلگمایر» همچنین خالق کتاب مصور «دراما» از کتاب‌های پرفروش نیویورک‌تایمز و یکی از ده کتاب مصور برتر نوجوانان «یالسا» است. کتاب دوم این سه گانه با عنوان: «خواهرها»؛ و کتاب سوم ... هنوز ترجمه نشده است؛ ا. شربیانی</span>
  <a data-text-id="9884821662741721492" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_303011864" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/303011864" />
    <a title="Seth T." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/160319-seth-t"><img alt="Seth T." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1251915636p2/160319.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/303011864?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Seth T." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Seth T." href="/user/show/160319-seth-t">Seth T.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/160319-seth-t?shelf=comics">comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer303011864" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2910151659451665252"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380373650i/727311.jpg' alt='Smile by Raina Telgemeier' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Braces sucked. From sixth through the beginning of eighth grade, I wore braces. Not brackets, but bands. On every tooth. Errant wires carved totems of the soft tissue at the back of my jaw—sacred designs that I'm sure exist there to this day. My smiles looked of cold steel. My jaw hurt from aggressive application of rubber bands. And my teeth would not get clean. At the end of those two years, I had the perfect smile—or at least the perfect teeth with which to perform that kind of smile had I kn</span>
  <span id="freeText2910151659451665252" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380373650i/727311.jpg" alt="Smile by Raina Telgemeier" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Braces sucked. From sixth through the beginning of eighth grade, I wore braces. Not brackets, but bands. On every tooth. Errant wires carved totems of the soft tissue at the back of my jaw—sacred designs that I'm sure exist there to this day. My smiles looked of cold steel. My jaw hurt from aggressive application of rubber bands. And my teeth would not get clean. At the end of those two years, I had the perfect smile—or at least the perfect teeth with which to perform that kind of smile had I known how to do such a thing in eighth grade. A quarter-century later and I still have the physical tools with which to enact the perfect smile <i>as well as</i> something of the social gearwork to make my attempts less ghastly. Braces, for me, worked their magic. And I'm still not sure it was worth it.<br><br>Still, regardless of how difficult my own experience was, those pains, miseries, and woes pale when compared to the manifold sorrows with which Raina Telgemeier's young life was cursed. The author, when she was in sixth grade, fell and did substantial damage to her two front teeth. Knocked one out and smashed the other one up into the gumline. I'm getting queasy just writing about it because as Telgemeier relates the event and immediate aftermath in her autobio comic, <i>Smile</i>, the whole experience is rather harrowing. I'm not usually one to blanch at grusome displays of violence in either prose or comics or film or art. Caravaggio's <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Caravaggio_Judith_Beheading_Holofernes.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">Judith</a> leaves me nonplussed. Murakami's manskinner in <i>The Wind-Up Bird Chronicle</i> is exciting but never nauseating. And the cannibalistic humour in <i>
  <a href="http://goodokbad.com/index.php/reviews/chew_volume_1_review" rel="nofollow noopener">Chew</a>
</i> is merely amusing. But Telgemeier's recountment of her accident, the blood, the immediate visit to the dental surgeon, the x-rays showing where her missing tooth went—it all made me a bit faint.<br><br>Fortunately, all that was just the first fifteen pages or so. After that, <i>Smile</i> shifts into something not dissimilar to the common Young Adult exploration of junior-high– and then high-school–insecurities. The drama of growing up and all that. Only: young Raina also has much more orthodontic work in her immediate future than would the average kid suffering the slings and arrows of burgeoning puberty. Telgemeier balances the telling between school drama and mouth drama nicely—though it helps the reader to know that this is not just a story but that it is Telgemeier's story. Through Raina, the author relives a streamlined and story-driven version of her own life and makes it palatable for general audiences.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380373650i/727312.jpg" alt="Smile by Raina Telgemeier" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If I have one complaint about the book, it's that its lessons seem too pat, its morals too well-placed. The whole experience is very After School Special—not in that this is a story ineptly told (for Telgemeier is obviously well-skilled and the book well-crafted), but simply because everything fits together so very nicely. Which we don't often come to expect from biography. Lives are too messy to be retold so crisply. Of course, it may be possible that Telgemeier really lives in the sweetness that lifts so pleasantly from <i>Smile</i>'s pages. To that, then, my criticism is not so much that the history Telgemeier relates is not believable, but instead that it's just not complicated enough. It doesn't leave much for the reader to think on once the last page is turned.<br><br>But that most likely wasn't Teglemeier's intent and her audience plausibly isn't a cynical guy who's more than twenty years older than <i>Smile</i>'s principle figure. So make of that what you will.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380373650i/727313.jpg" alt="Smile by Raina Telgemeier" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>To its fortune, <i>Smile</i> is a brisk read for all its pages and will keep most readers interested enough to finish the book in a single sitting. The book paces well and even the pieces that seemed familiar or predictable always escape feeling formulaic or contrived. And Telgemeier makes Raina into a sympathetic character who, even when at her most pathetic or bratty, is someone you kind of just want to hold on to and take care of.<br><br>Telgemeier's art is lively and fluid and she seems to have little trouble putting her characters into whatever circumstance her story demands of them. Most impressive to me was how she allows her characters to age visibly. Raina begins as a small girl involved in Girl's Scouts, but soon makes the transition to junior high and then across that gulf of development into high school. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380373650i/727314.jpg" alt="Smile by Raina Telgemeier" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Telgemeier uses numerous visual cues to help us keep Raina's age straight. More than just the eventual appearance of breasts (the lazy artist's cue of choice), Raina's face, hair, and carriage all shift naturally as she matures. In the final pages, as her ordeal comes to a close, she has apparently grown up and has transitioned from childhood into young womanhood. <br><br>I had trouble deciding whether <i>Smile</i> was Good or just Ok. At the end of the day, the book really is something of a trifle, an entertaining yarn that sits pretty firmly in the YA tradition of non-challenging reads. But simultaneously, Telgemeier does a good job at what she sets out to do and the care with which she treats her characters is evident throughout. And while <i>Smile</i> is ostensibly about overcoming a dental crisis, it also explores our common inability to be happy due to our common inadequacies. <i>Smile</i> points out that our reliance upon the things that sour us to life is often entrenched simply because those things are comfortable. In any case, while to adults <i>Smile</i> may just be an entertaining read, to its targeted demographic the book may read like a manual to no longer being miserable.<br>________________<br><br><i>[Review courtesy of <a href="http://goodokbad.com/index.php/reviews/smile_review" rel="nofollow noopener">Good Ok Bad</a>]</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="2910151659451665252" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7720978560470284342">One of my worst nightmares is breaking or losing my teeth. I had braces for years, and had the orthodontist accidentally crack one of my teeth when he was polishing them up after I got my braces off. It haunts me to this day. <br/><br/>Raina tells the story of her own dental trauma-drama with this delightfully drawn graphic novel that lays bare not only the horror of dealing with the braces, the fake teeth, the retainers after her accident, but also frankly reveals her awkwardness, loneliness, and nerdine</span>
  <span id="freeText7720978560470284342" style="display:none">One of my worst nightmares is breaking or losing my teeth. I had braces for years, and had the orthodontist accidentally crack one of my teeth when he was polishing them up after I got my braces off. It haunts me to this day. <br /><br />Raina tells the story of her own dental trauma-drama with this delightfully drawn graphic novel that lays bare not only the horror of dealing with the braces, the fake teeth, the retainers after her accident, but also frankly reveals her awkwardness, loneliness, and nerdiness in jr high and beginning high school. The changes of puberty. Having crushes on boys who never look at you, while accidentally offending nice boys who do like you. Mean friends, good friends, and unexpected friends, it's all here. This is a wonderful book!<br /><br />2018: My daughter, Baby Girl, got this for her ninth birthday a few months ago. Yesterday I asked her how many times she has read it. It's more than five, but less than ten, apparently. So I had to reread it myself, and wow, I had forgotten how great it was, and how it's not just about her teeth, but her life, her friendships, her school struggles. </span>

<div id="review_97735278" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Jennifer Rayment" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3123013-jennifer-rayment"><img alt="Jennifer Rayment" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1264700209p2/3123013.jpg" /></a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/97735278?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Rayment" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Rayment" href="/user/show/3123013-jennifer-rayment">Jennifer Rayment</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer97735278" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13892815642047648034">Jake's Review: Um Mom, this is like a girls book, do I really have to read it. Come on Jake, just try a few pages and tell me what you think. 1 hour later. Mom this is pretty good for a girls book, but I hope I never have to wear braces. It doesn't sound like its much fun and btw girls are gross! The pictures are very funny and I like that she plays video games. I didn't like the drawings of when she broke her teeth because there was too much blood -- ICKY!. I don't think my friends would like t</span>
  <span id="freeText13892815642047648034" style="display:none">Jake's Review: Um Mom, this is like a girls book, do I really have to read it. Come on Jake, just try a few pages and tell me what you think. 1 hour later. Mom this is pretty good for a girls book, but I hope I never have to wear braces. It doesn't sound like its much fun and btw girls are gross! The pictures are very funny and I like that she plays video games. I didn't like the drawings of when she broke her teeth because there was too much blood -- ICKY!. I don't think my friends would like this book because they are boys and boys don't like to read girls stuff. Also I think this book is for older kids because they are talking about liking boys and other icky girls stuff. I don't like that her friends made fun of her for having braces. You shouldnt tease people (Mom's note, he said this 1 hour after teasing his 17 mth old brother) its just not nice. I like the authors drawing and the way she told the story, but I would have liked it better if it was about a boy my age. You can bring me more graphic novel though ok -- much more fun to read than books!<br />Rating: 7/10 (I know I am surprised he gave it such a high rating)<br /><br />Mom's Review: I honestly didn't think Jake was going to finish this book, figured he would just read a couple of pages and than give up. Surprised that he read it all and gave me a review on it, I am very proud of him for sticking through it. I absolutely loved this graphic novel, eventhough it brought back many painful memories of my own experience with having braces. This graphic novel is sort of like a cross between a Judy Blume novel and a For Better or Worse comic. The story is written with tons of humour and portrays the awkwardness of being a teen extremely effectively. The story is fast paced, realistic and I think would appeal to the reluctant reader as well as most pre-teen and teen readers. Definately required reading for those who have or have had braces. I think it would be great if all Orthodentists had a copy of this in their offices -- and a few of them REALLY should read it (They might even learn how to be a little more sympathetic with their patients). The underlying message of encouraging us to focus more on what we are on the inside rather than how we look on the outside is very sublty done and not at all preachy. <br />Rating: 10/10<br /></span>

<div id="review_268536364" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/268536364" />
    <a title="Erika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7485530-erika"><img alt="Erika" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1327105245p2/7485530.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/268536364?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erika" href="/user/show/7485530-erika">Erika</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780545132060" href="/book/show/6764756-smile">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer268536364" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9552802655980090315">This book was very… cute. I had braces for seven years so could I relate to the protagonist’s dental woes? Yes. Was I necessarily engaged while reading? No. I give this book credit where credit is due, I’m sure to a younger audience, perhaps going through what Raina was (to one extent or another) would enjoy the book more than I did. I expect more from the books I read, especially graphic novels, than what was presented here. I found it very basic. <br/><br/>As a reader, I wasn’t hugely impressed. There w</span>
  <span id="freeText9552802655980090315" style="display:none">This book was very… cute. I had braces for seven years so could I relate to the protagonist’s dental woes? Yes. Was I necessarily engaged while reading? No. I give this book credit where credit is due, I’m sure to a younger audience, perhaps going through what Raina was (to one extent or another) would enjoy the book more than I did. I expect more from the books I read, especially graphic novels, than what was presented here. I found it very basic. <br /><br />As a reader, I wasn’t hugely impressed. There was no complexity. I could see what was coming and apart from occasionally getting upset with her friends I did not get emotionally involved. It was a quick read and it was over before I really noticed but not in the way that completely engrosses you as a reader, just that the story was so much like a glorified comic strip it flew by.<br /><br />As a teacher, I would probably have this in my classroom library. I would keep it in case a student was a struggling reader, or if I wanted an example of a graphic novel (though I feel I can keep better examples than this). I would not consider teaching it. I intend to teach high school and as such I would hope this would be a little below their level.<br /><br />I would recommend this to an early middle school student or a child I knew was about to get braces to sort of ease their worries about what was going to happen to them. I don’t think I would recommend it to anyone solely on literary merit.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9552802655980090315" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=families">families</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer16088645153412147126">Touching, intensely personally relatable and while of course not as in-depth as I would have expected and needed in a non graphic novel, Raina Telgemeier's <u>Smile</u> has both hit the spot for me and brought forth many pleasant and sometimes also not so pleasant memories. For while I might not have experienced (and this thankfully) the kind of dental and orthodontial nightmares that Raina Telgemeier obviously had to endure as a young teenager, I can and do very much empathise and understand, as a ver</span>
  <span id="freeText16088645153412147126" style="display:none">Touching, intensely personally relatable and while of course not as in-depth as I would have expected and needed in a non graphic novel, Raina Telgemeier's <u>Smile</u> has both hit the spot for me and brought forth many pleasant and sometimes also not so pleasant memories. For while I might not have experienced (and this thankfully) the kind of dental and orthodontial nightmares that Raina Telgemeier obviously had to endure as a young teenager, I can and do very much empathise and understand, as a very close school friend did in fact have to go through pretty much the same scenarios as Raina did (even having to deal with and face incompetence in the form of a supremely clueless dental technician who used much too little freezing on my friend's mouth before a painful extraction) and well, Raina's family dynamics actually in many ways do mirror my own (including having a younger sister with whom I have never managed to all that much emotionally and philosophically connect), not to mention the tried but true, painful learning experience and dictum that "with friends like this one does not really need enemies" namely that bullying and teasing from one's supposed friends and companions is not healthy and not something to accept and swallow as though nothing untoward had occurred (an evocatively lovely even if sometimes chafing with regard to personal and not all that enjoyable remembrances reading experience is <u>Smile</u>, but really the pain is almost as exquisite as the pleasure, and perhaps even more heartfelt and authentic). <br /><br />Four stars (rounded up to a full five stars, as I have indeed very much enjoyed if not loved both narrative and illustrations and been really and truly touched by Raina Telgemeier's delightfully frank openness, and heck, as a person of German extraction and language instructor, I cannot help but wax poetic about the scene where Raina is obviously taking German at school and that the relevant illustrations actually have ALL of the German language words spelled with no grammar or orthographical mistakes).</span>
  <a data-text-id="16088645153412147126" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_246377311" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Mallika Sankaran" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7170873-mallika-sankaran"><img alt="Mallika Sankaran" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/246377311?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mallika Sankaran" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mallika Sankaran" href="/user/show/7170873-mallika-sankaran">Mallika Sankaran</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer246377311" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17486046109706379735">Smile by Raina Telgemeier is a realistic fiction graphic novel. It is a true story about the author herself. It was nominated for a Red Dot Award in 2011-2012.<br/><br/> It tells the story of Raina's life from middle school to high school. You might think that a book just about middle school and high school is boring but not when the unexpected happens. In this book, it's when Raina falls down one day as she is running back home when her two front teeth fall out as they smash against the ground. From brac</span>
  <span id="freeText17486046109706379735" style="display:none">Smile by Raina Telgemeier is a realistic fiction graphic novel. It is a true story about the author herself. It was nominated for a Red Dot Award in 2011-2012.<br /><br /> It tells the story of Raina's life from middle school to high school. You might think that a book just about middle school and high school is boring but not when the unexpected happens. In this book, it's when Raina falls down one day as she is running back home when her two front teeth fall out as they smash against the ground. From braces to headgear to even root canals, Raina tells us how she survives school.<br /><br />I think this a really good and interesting book. It's good because many of us middle school girls can relate to it. I felt I could relate to it because I have braces right now and I know how that experience is. <br /><br />It also keeps you engaged making you want to read the whole book in one day. Once you start this book, there's no stopping. The events keep hooking you because event after event there are interesting things.<br /><br />Raina illustrates and describes the scenes really well because you can actually step into the character's shoes and start to live their life and see how they feel about things. I feel even though this is a comic book, the imagery is very good because you can dream about yourself in that situation.<br /><br /><br /> I would probably recommend this to middle school girls as it's mostly a girl book and they type of situations are what we can relate to in real life. It's also quite easy to understand and easy to follow the story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17486046109706379735" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3240464523" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3240464523" />
    <a title="Briar&#39;s Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32054036-briar-s-reviews"><img alt="Briar&#39;s Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402183274p2/32054036.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3240464523?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Briar&#39;s Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Briar&#39;s Reviews" href="/user/show/32054036-briar-s-reviews">Briar&#39;s Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=art">art</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=top-books">top-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=cute">cute</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=fun">fun</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=guilty-pleasure">guilty-pleasure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3240464523" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9314907080598793421">Smile by Raina Telgemeier is a story that totally connected with me in ways other books couldn't. Raina's story echoes a lot of my own, and it made me feel all warm and fuzzy inside to see a story like this get shared. Many kids will face dental issues and bullying, so a book like this could do wonders for them!<br/><br/>I saw this book years ago and wanted to pick it up but never did. Recently, I found it at a local book store on sale and decided this was the time for me to grab it. I also just wanted so</span>
  <span id="freeText9314907080598793421" style="display:none">Smile by Raina Telgemeier is a story that totally connected with me in ways other books couldn't. Raina's story echoes a lot of my own, and it made me feel all warm and fuzzy inside to see a story like this get shared. Many kids will face dental issues and bullying, so a book like this could do wonders for them!<br /><br />I saw this book years ago and wanted to pick it up but never did. Recently, I found it at a local book store on sale and decided this was the time for me to grab it. I also just wanted some more cute graphic novels in my life, so that helped a lot.<br /><br />I was honestly surprised how addicting and easy to read this book was. Yes, middle grade books tend to be easier for adults to read, but I found myself sinking into the story and not being able to get out. I related to it so much and I could totally feel for Raina. Middle school and high school are hard, especially when going through the pain of braces and surgeries (I for one, can attest to that). <br /><br />Some of the major positives of this book are as follows:<br />1. Raina shares a personal stories that many people can relate to. This story will hit many readers in ways they don't realize.<br /><br />2. The illustrations in this book was fun and colourful and kept me hooked to the story.<br /><br />3. The story was fast, easy to read, and quite fun (despite all the pain Raina was going through).<br /><br />4. Raina standing up to her bullies was a serious "high-five" moment for me. Go Raina! You do you, girl!<br /><br />5. There's lots of little references to my own childhood in this book, so I can totally see adults digging this book along with their kids. Seriously, this book can be read by "all ages". It's a great read!<br /><br />Negatives:<br />1. I didn't realize this book was a memoir at first. I'm not sure if it was obvious or if I just missed it. That's literally the only negative I can find. This book is great!<br /><br />In all honesty, I love this book. I would definitely recommend readers pick this book up for a little fun and a lot of nostalgia. Who doesn't forget those dreaded dentist appointments? Or if you were lucky enough to have braces, the craziness of those appointments! <br /><br />I will 100% be picking up any more books by Raina Telgemeier that I come across. <br /><br />Five out of five stars! </span>
  <a data-text-id="9314907080598793421" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_267769686" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/267769686" />
    <a title="Jessica Griggs" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7490884-jessica-griggs"><img alt="Jessica Griggs" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328473102p2/7490884.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/267769686?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica Griggs" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica Griggs" href="/user/show/7490884-jessica-griggs">Jessica Griggs</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer267769686" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14701293946496866143">At first, I didn't know what to expect from this book. When I got it, I opened it up and immediately saw pictures. Like the little kid that I am (a 13 yr old girl in a 21 yr old woman's body), I was immediately excited and ready to start. One of my favorite comic book/series is <u>Calvin and Hobbes</u>, so I was very eager to see what this book held between its pages. I was still curious, because I knew <u>Smile</u> held a different weight and focus than <u>Calvin and Hobbes</u>. I was not sure how a book full of pi</span>
  <span id="freeText14701293946496866143" style="display:none">At first, I didn't know what to expect from this book. When I got it, I opened it up and immediately saw pictures. Like the little kid that I am (a 13 yr old girl in a 21 yr old woman's body), I was immediately excited and ready to start. One of my favorite comic book/series is <u>Calvin and Hobbes</u>, so I was very eager to see what this book held between its pages. I was still curious, because I knew <u>Smile</u> held a different weight and focus than <u>Calvin and Hobbes</u>. I was not sure how a book full of pictures that make up one long comic strip could hold somewhat of the same ground as a non-graphic novel; until I realized that I had just finished possibly the funniest and touching book in about an hour and a half. I couldn't put it down, nor did I want to. What made it even better is the fact that this book is actually based off a true story and it actually happened.<br /><br />As a student, I felt every part of Raina's story. Since I went through the trial and error of braces, and even underwent the torturous and numerous variety of doctor visits, I completely sympathized with her. Other than her "vampire teeth", we pretty much had the same school life, which made her story completely relate-able. The only thing we didn't share was the earthquake experience. As I turned the pages, I found that I wasn't just reading a story about Raina, but about myself. I was watching me crush on two different boys, fighting with my sister, playing video games and being crushed by my "friends". I saw myself blossom from awkward middle schooler to high school/college student, through Raina. Honestly, I was laughing the whole time I read this book, between the exaggerated pictures and expressions to the language. I also laughed because I completely understood what she was going through, and as I made the journey with her, I was also laughing at a past me.<br /><br />As a teacher, without a doubt, I would teach this book. It would be a great seg-way between middle and high school. Also, students would be more inclined to read this book and understand it since they can see the words and the pictures together, almost like a still movie and the remote to go to the next scene is just them turning the page. Like myself, this book is also extremely relate-able. Students will want to read this book and they will connect with it more since it will be a lot of what they are going through, particularly the girls. This will be a definite addition to my in-class library as well!<br /><br />There is no doubt that I will be using this book in the future, and re-reading it in the near future as well. I also have a younger sister, and for a fact, she will be reading this book, especially if she goes into braces. I feel that this book helps make growing up a little less scary and a little more clear and realistic. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14701293946496866143" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_355269995" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/355269995" />
    <a title="Josh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/844382-josh"><img alt="Josh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452975129p2/844382.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/355269995?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Josh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Josh" href="/user/show/844382-josh">Josh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/844382-josh?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/844382-josh?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/844382-josh?shelf=ya-kids">ya-kids</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer355269995" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12935876837189198974">I saw this book in the orthodontist's office while I was awaiting my appointment to be fitted with braces. It's ostensibly aimed at adolescent/teenage girls--which as an adult male, I am not--but in my vulnerable state of anxiety and meek submissiveness I thought the book still might be a source of comfort. Good news: it was! I got a library copy later to give it a more thorough reading, and really enjoyed it. <br/><br/>Raina goes through a whole lot more than I should ever have to. After an accident, she</span>
  <span id="freeText12935876837189198974" style="display:none">I saw this book in the orthodontist's office while I was awaiting my appointment to be fitted with braces. It's ostensibly aimed at adolescent/teenage girls--which as an adult male, I am not--but in my vulnerable state of anxiety and meek submissiveness I thought the book still might be a source of comfort. Good news: it was! I got a library copy later to give it a more thorough reading, and really enjoyed it. <br /><br />Raina goes through a whole lot more than I should ever have to. After an accident, she undergoes years of braces, headgear, sadistic periodontists, and associated teenage drama. I merely have to correct what my dentist calls "occlusal disharmony"--a misaligned bite that has steadily worn down many of my teeth into a state of fragility. And I don't have to do it as a teenager. <br /><br />I could still relate. While I'm not the same age as Raina the book character, I *am* the same age as Raina the author. A small but important example: early on, she escaped bad days by playing Nintendo (one panel even has a lovingly re-created final screenshot from Super Mario Bros. 2). It's probably true for a huge percentage of Class of '95ers, but old school NES definitely makes me feel like I'm safe and happy at home. The larger point, made very effectively as Raina negotiates various dental and social trials, is that there are both important and unimportant influences on your happiness and self-esteem.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12935876837189198974" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_298333502" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/298333502" />
    <a title="Sesana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana"><img alt="Sesana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413088169p2/5172893.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/298333502?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sesana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sesana" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana">Sesana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=comics">comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer298333502" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13271012215033640113">I feel like Smile might be a good book to give to a girl who's just found out that she's going to need braces and is feeling down about it. Very likely, she'll have it a lot easier than poor Raina did. This is the author's own story about what she went through with her teeth. It must be true, because nobody would make this up. It's a fun read, when I wasn't squirming with sympathy pain. The art is cute and cartoony, possibly because anything realistic would make this just too gruesome. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

Raina's parents were loving and supportive and Raina was part of a group of friends for a long time who constantly made fun of her. Eventually she realized the best thing to do was leave them and find new friends who accepted her for who she was.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1474834641i/20646069._SY540_.jpg" width="435" height="640" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>I think I would have loved this when I was thirteen.</b></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5493392335706886464"><br/><br/>I thoroughly enjoyed this graphic novel by Raina Telgemeier; such a fast-paced and fun read with colorful drawings. <br/>The aspect I enjoyed most about Smile, is the fact that this is Raina's actual life story. We get to see her going through a tough time with lots of dental work and braces in her childhood and adolescence.   <span id="freeText5493392335706886464" style="display:none"><br /><br />I thoroughly enjoyed this graphic novel by Raina Telgemeier; such a fast-paced and fun read with colorful drawings. <br />The aspect I enjoyed most about Smile, is the fact that this is Raina's actual life story. Plus, a major earthquake, and boy and mean girl drama. <br />Her "friends" were kind of awful to her all along, and I just kept waiting for her to realize they were not worth it. <br />It's nice to see that after she went through all that painful dental work, Raina's smile turned out looking pretty good; which we can see at last page of the book! <br />Really recommend this read to anyone who's looking to read a graphic novel or simply a really entertaining story!</span>

<div id="review_1824200963" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1824200963" />
    <a title="Brierly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25485458-brierly"><img alt="Brierly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421634217p2/25485458.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1824200963?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brierly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brierly" href="/user/show/25485458-brierly">Brierly</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25485458-brierly?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25485458-brierly?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25485458-brierly?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25485458-brierly?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1824200963" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15484774617955764205"><i>Smile</i> is a multi-genre offering from Raina Telgemeier: it is a memoir of her childhood, it is a graphic novel, and it is directed at a middle grades audience. <i>Smile</i> covers the beginning, middle, and conclusion of a particularly gruesome, non-fatal (it is a memoir, after all) accident in which Raina trips and breaks/knocks out several of her teeth early into her sixth grade year. This is a classic coming-of-age moment, coupled with an exploration of family life. The sequel, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18225810.Sisters' title='Sisters by Raina Telgemeier' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sisters</a>, will likely o</span>
  <span id="freeText15484774617955764205" style="display:none"><i>Smile</i> is a multi-genre offering from Raina Telgemeier: it is a memoir of her childhood, it is a graphic novel, and it is directed at a middle grades audience. <i>Smile</i> covers the beginning, middle, and conclusion of a particularly gruesome, non-fatal (it is a memoir, after all) accident in which Raina trips and breaks/knocks out several of her teeth early into her sixth grade year. This is a classic coming-of-age moment, coupled with an exploration of family life. The sequel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18225810.Sisters" title="Sisters by Raina Telgemeier" rel="nofollow noopener">Sisters</a>, will likely offer more information when I get around to it.<br /><br />Excellent writing and illustration, ESPECIALLY noting that Telgemeier herself is the sole artist. This is relatively rare for graphic novels, and the personal weight of the narrative becomes all the more vibrant because of Telgemeier's truth-telling. If you are looking for what's hot right now in middle grades, look no further than Telgemeier's body of work (oh, and check out <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/326609.Kwame_Alexander" title="Kwame Alexander" rel="nofollow noopener">Kwame Alexander</a>!)</span>
  <a data-text-id="15484774617955764205" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1774210472" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1774210472" />
    <a title="Emily O" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59573339-emily-o"><img alt="Emily O" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1488901976p2/59573339.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1774210472?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily O" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily O" href="/user/show/59573339-emily-o">Emily O</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59573339-emily-o?shelf=first-9-weeks">first-9-weeks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1774210472" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4294954857415165178"><i>Smile</i> is one of those books that you could read in 3 days! BUT ITS AMAZING! This is probably my favorite book I've read so far! <i>Smile</i> is about a girl named Raina, who knocks her tooth out after girl scouts. They go through the longest process to get that tooth fixed including braces, retainer, fake tooth, and surgery. During the process a lot of other things happen. Raina loses some friends and gains some friends. She even get her ears pierced. But most importantly, she starts middle school! " D</span>
  <span id="freeText4294954857415165178" style="display:none"><i>Smile</i> is one of those books that you could read in 3 days! BUT ITS AMAZING! This is probably my favorite book I've read so far! <i>Smile</i> is about a girl named Raina, who knocks her tooth out after girl scouts. They go through the longest process to get that tooth fixed including braces, retainer, fake tooth, and surgery. During the process a lot of other things happen. Raina loses some friends and gains some friends. She even get her ears pierced. But most importantly, she starts middle school! " Dun dun dun" Starting middle school didn't go as well as when I started. Boys were bullies, pimples, someone even pulled down her pants during lunch. And her birthday was an even bigger disaster. All of her friends turned on her. How will she overcome this mess? You'll have to read and find out! This book is a graphic novel so if you liked <i>Drama</i>, or <i>Sisters</i>then you will love this book like I did! While you're reading this book you will be saying to yourself " No Raina thats a bad idea!" or " Awwww pore Raina!" This book is filled with so many twists and turns. This book made me feel sad, happy, and a little bit angry. But overall this book was really fun to read. I can't wait for this author to come out with more books just like this one!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4294954857415165178" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="M.  [storme reads a lot]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="M.  [storme reads a lot]" href="/user/show/11748214-m-storme-reads-a-lot">M.  [storme reads a lot]</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11748214-m-storme-reads-a-lot?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3070136152" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13723779439512693045">Raina writes such cute books. The drawings are fantastic. I love how she uses her own life to bring her art to life. These are the types of books middle grade readers need! I love them because I recall those times with mixed emotions. I think nowadays they are useful so kids know they aren’t alone in the world. This book talks about braces, finding friends who respect you, and first crushes. Seeing these subjects in books is so good for kids now so they know what emotions and experiences they ar</span>
  <span id="freeText13723779439512693045" style="display:none">Raina writes such cute books. The drawings are fantastic. I love how she uses her own life to bring her art to life. These are the types of books middle grade readers need! I love them because I recall those times with mixed emotions. I think nowadays they are useful so kids know they aren’t alone in the world. This book talks about braces, finding friends who respect you, and first crushes. Seeing these subjects in books is so good for kids now so they know what emotions and experiences they are having is normal! I’d definitely recommend these to preteen readers or anyone looking for a fun graphic novel,</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TM3D+4BWHWg/mB6PVW8TnkuaWLYGsZPHZatTp+8t7dgd42WQXT48S8nIZ6p95Qtr4PgV1jEvet85JDWx9hfP/w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('iO+E546actD+cRnM0q2GVLkSf7P6ydMwcfDrtqBpTTfZwSKMU/JT8wghYOn6J56hEnAy081XOigtf42guVNvEA==')})
  }
//]]>
